**[02:54:36] WIL:** Hey nerds, I'm Wil Wheaton, I know right? And guess what? It is back.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** International Tabletop Day has returned, this year on April 11th.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** What is that, you say? What is Tabletop Day? Well, if you don't know, then shame on you.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** International Tabletop Day is a worldwide celebration dedicated to the tabletop games we love to play with the people we love.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** People we like, people we've never even met before, it doesn't matter, last year we had over 3,000 registered events across seven continents and over 80 countries, that is amazing! But this year we're going to make it even bigger.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** "Will Wheaton, how can we make it even bigger than last year?" That's what she said.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** Start now.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** Trend #TabletopDay on Twitter, because that was awesome.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** Broadcast your plans on the internet, make a video, share pictures, start a blog, create a dating profile for other sexy gamers in your area, whatever you want.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** Celebrate it in your own way, but we wanna hear from you.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** Be sure to use #TabletopDay, or @TabletopDay to let us know.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** It is up to you, world.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** Visit TabletopDay.com to register your event, or find one near you.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** You can also download exclusive content and check out some of our favorite games.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** We will be streaming our own live event, here in Los Angeles for you to watch.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** And there will be more on that soon.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** You love tabletop games, and we love you, so join us in the global celebration, on April 11th.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** Play more games.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** Hey everybody, I'm Wil Wheaton, and I am coming to you semi-live from the Twitch TV set here at the Geek & Sundry stages in beautiful downtown Burbank, California.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** I am here to tell you everything you ever wanted to know about Tabletop's RPG show, coming this June, but were afraid to ask.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** Or have been asking for close to a year and I've been saying, "We'll tell you at some point in the future." You can consider this the big announcement.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** It was incredibly difficult to cast this show.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** We needed people who were very comfortable improvising, who had experience playing role playing games, and who were available when we planned to shoot the show.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** It was surprisingly difficult to get a pool of people who fit all of those criteria, and choose the most awesome among them.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** So your cast playing in this wonderful show are: Yuri Lowenthal, Laura Bailey, Hank Green, and Alison Haislip.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** I'm really excited to have these people all together.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** They're all my friends, they are all wonderful storytellers, and they are going to be a tremendous party of adventurers.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** I'm only gonna try to kill them a little bit.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** The most frequently asked question since I announced that there was going to be a Tabletop RPG show is, hey Wil Wheaton! Why are you so awesome? The second most frequently asked question is, what system are you using to power this game? First and foremost, I needed a system that was going to support the way I play roleplaying games, and that is telling a story collaboratively with a group of players with me as the GM.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** I looked at some very well known systems like Dungeons & Dragons, and Savage Worlds, I looked at systems that I love, like Fate Core, and I even looked at the True 20, a d20 modern system.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** And I really wanted to use something that was released by an independent publisher.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** I wanted to bring something to the forefront of the roleplaying world that maybe not as many people are familiar with as I want them to be.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** But I wanna play the way that I played when I was falling in love with roleplaying games when I was a kid.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** I wanna be able to sit around on a couch and some chairs with my friends, not have to worry about a map on a table in front of us, and just work together to use our imaginations to tell a story.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** But there's a system that I really love that's elegant, it's easy to learn, it's easy to teach, it's very easy to understand, and it really just gets out of the way when you want to tell a story together.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** And that is the Adventure Game Engine that Green Ronin Publishing used to drive the Dragon Age tabletop roleplaying game.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** I asked the developer three years ago to please make generic, so that we can build a setting and put on top of it.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** They said actually this is something we really wanna do.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** And it's come together.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** We have been able to work together with Green Ronin to develop the fantasy Adventure Game Engine.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** This is gonna take a lot of the things you know from the Dragon Age RPG, and put it all together to support our world, which I have had the best time creating.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** I sat down three months ago with some amazing writers, and just started brainstorming about what kind of world we wanted to explore.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** But what I kept coming back to is, I love science fiction, and I love fantasy.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** Why not put them together? Why not build a world that is inspired by the 1978 Heavy Metal movie, and 1980's amazing Saturday morning cartoon show, Thundarr the Barbarian.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** I thought it would be great for characters to encounter goblinoid kind of creatures, and instead of them using crossbows, they're using laser rifles.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** I've got it all worked out, we have a huge team of writers that put all this together that built an amazing codex that gave terrific logic to all of these decisions that we made.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** We're not gonna tell you what they are.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** You may discover some of them during the course of the season.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** So what is the name of this incredible world? The title of our show is Titansgrave: The Ashes of Valkana.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** You can sort of come up with your own ideas about what those words mean.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** I know, but I'm not telling.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** 'Cause that's not how the Wheaton talks.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** Titansgrave: The Ashes of Valkana will premiere right here at Geekandsundry.com on June 2nd.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** For those of you not in America, Titansgrave: The Ashes of Valkana will premiere right here on Geek & Sundry on two June.

**[02:54:36] WIL:** So I hope that you're as excited about this as I am, and I hope that you will tune in, and then watch us for ten straight weeks of incredible high adventure story telling, and until then, play more games.

**[03:14:38] MATT:** Yeah, they do definitely matter.

**[03:14:38] MATT:** A couple quick answers here.

**[03:14:38] MATT:** The conversion from Pathfinder to Fifth Edition was decided because, as we're going on to this show, and we had so many players, combat tends to get bogged down, and a lot of floating modifiers in Pathfinder.

**[03:14:38] MATT:** For large groups like this it's difficult to keep it flowing and moving.

**[03:14:38] MATT:** I felt once I had taken a look at Fifth Edition, that the combat system was a little more simplified, and a little easier to make freeform and just roll with it.

**[03:14:38] MATT:** So that was a much better decision.

**[03:14:38] MATT:** Plus Dungeons & Dragons generally has a better name recognition than Pathfinder, so when you're putting a show out there, it's probably easier to do with very minimal transition, it took a little bit of customizing, like for Percy's gunslinger.

**[03:14:38] MATT:** We just had to customize it, we made it ourselves.

**[03:14:38] MATT:** We sat down.

**[03:15:18] TALIESIN:** Took a day.

**[03:15:18] MATT:** Took a day, and we worked out, some of the stuff we wanted to keep, some of the things that didn't break it, we wanted to make it interesting.

**[03:15:18] MATT:** It is a martial archetype for the fighter class.

**[03:15:18] MATT:** So it does give the bonus a fighter class does.

**[03:15:18] MATT:** Nothing is too overpowered about it, other than just having custom weapons, and some cool grit-based abilities that we kinda transferred over from Pathfinder.

**[03:15:18] MATT:** It's interesting.

**[03:15:18] MATT:** It's a good challenge to see how it works out.

**[03:15:41] TALIESIN:** It is, it's working out.

**[03:15:41] TALIESIN:** I'm digging it.

**[03:15:41] TALIESIN:** I keep reading and finding things I'm not doing that could be more interesting, so.

**[03:16:14] MATT:** I answered that a second ago.

**[03:16:16] LIAM:** Oh, you did?

**[03:16:16] MATT:** Yeah, the idea being that the reason we switched was it was easier for large-scale combat, and the system was a little more simplified, and I felt for such a large party it'd be easier to do.

**[03:16:16] MATT:** Plus character creation for any guests we have in the future, so that was the main reason.

**[03:16:16] MATT:** I love Pathfinder, but at this size, it's good.

**[03:16:16] MATT:** Answering your earlier question too, I saw someone ask, a good party size.

**[03:16:16] MATT:** Legitimately, my preference is between four and six players.

**[03:16:16] MATT:** This works because they're amazing players, and because we keep it very freeform, and not getting bogged down in minutia too often.

**[03:16:16] MATT:** The four to six players I think is a good sweet spot.

**[03:25:17] LIAM:** Connected to that, someone asked, if you had any tips, and I'd like to know the answer to this too, because I'm running a game for my eight-year-old son and his friends who are about to start, do you have any tips for new DM's?

**[03:25:28] MATT:** Yes.

**[03:25:28] MATT:** Let's see.

**[03:25:28] MATT:** I could do a whole panel on that.

**[03:25:28] MATT:** Tips for new DMs.

**[03:25:28] MATT:** Preparation is important.

**[03:25:28] MATT:** You wanna outline cities, come up with ideas for NPCs, that you think would be essential to a story, or like people that really run elements of the town.

**[03:25:28] MATT:** Simple notes can be like, they're this race, this is their disposition, if you have a particular voice you wanna try for, make a note of this kind of voice.

**[03:25:28] MATT:** So whenever you come back to them you have a reminder.

**[03:25:28] MATT:** And spend a lot of time building that structure, you don't have to be too detailed.

**[03:25:28] MATT:** Always leave room to play in the world, because you never know what your players are gonna do.

**[03:25:28] MATT:** Be prepared to improv.

**[03:25:28] MATT:** I prefer loose preparation, and then just kinda rolling where the players take you.

**[03:26:10] LIAM:** Although you wrote a monologue for Clarence, right? Because that was very intricate.

**[03:26:10] LIAM:** We were all just ready--

**[03:26:16] ASHLEY:** Yeah, there's no way you just thought that up.

**[03:26:19] MATT:** There are certain elements, part of the notes I take is for certain NPCs I'll write down key information that they know, and depending on how you ask them, what you say to them, and what you try and extract from them, they might give you some of the information, they might not, if you coerce them, or intimidate them.

**[03:26:19] MATT:** Or if they're willing to give up the information, I have all that written down.

**[03:26:19] MATT:** So for that information today, you guys were asking him, and since you allied with Clarence, he was willing to discuss with you.

**[03:26:19] MATT:** So I had all that prewritten, but depending on how much you said, it was what you guys asked.

**[03:26:51] LIAM:** Do you have random encounters ready, in case we're like, "ah, fuck it, I don't wanna go down to the dungeon, I wanna go back up and beat up some dwarves." Do you have shit kind of ready?

**[03:41:38] MATT:** So here's how I run the world.

**[03:41:38] MATT:** I feel that one of the problems in some RPGs is that death becomes flippant when magic allows you to completely undo it.

**[03:41:38] MATT:** In my campaigns certain powerful spells like Greater Restoration, Resurrection, things like that are a challenge, meaning you can definitely undo death, but a lot of it is based on your capabilities as a spellcaster, your attachment to the people you've been traveling with.

**[03:41:38] MATT:** So if ever a character does die, a resurrection can be attempted, but it is a challenge.

**[03:41:38] MATT:** Which means there's a possibility of it failing.

**[03:41:38] MATT:** In which case, if the resurrection fails, the soul is lost, the character is permanently dead.

**[03:41:38] MATT:** The player then can leave and never come back if they want to, but they have the option to create a new character, and be reintroduced to the campaign like half a level lower than the rest.
